HORIZONTAL WELL

Well File # 30467
Dear Elizabeth:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 25103, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on the
condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries
and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 25 & 36 T144N R97W. Tool
error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be
maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-
back whenever filtration operations are conducted. OXY USA Inc. must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety
Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28
(Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any
producing well or oil tank." Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location. In
cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface owner
of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite
spacing/drilling unit. OXY USA INC must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is: 429'S. Also, based on the azimuth of the
proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10574'S and 797'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The
following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and
time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-
8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Elizabeth S. Bush-Ivie, P.E.
January 14, 2015
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified copy
of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a
form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Stae 4-25-36H-144-97

COMPASS 5000.1 Build 72
OXY USA INC.
MIDCONTINENT BUSINESS UNIT
WILLISTON DIVISION
GAS CAPTURE PLAN
KARY SWSE 24 PAD
SECTION 24-T144N-R97W
DUNN COUNTY, NORTH DAKOTA
WELLS
KARY 6-24-13H-144-97
STATE 4-25-36H-144-97
OCTOBER 13, 2014
Pad
The two wells that will be located on the Kary SWSE 24 Pad are shown in the table below.
Pipeline Notification
These wells will be connected to ONEOK's low pressure gathering system in Dunn County,
North Dakota. Oxy's acreage that comprises the spacing units (SU) for the Kary 6-24-13H-144-
97 and State 4-25-36H-144-97 is dedicated to ONEOK. Under terms of the contract, ONEOK is
obligated to install the facilities that are required to connect these wells to its gathering system.
Oxy provides (on a monthly basis) to ONEOK a drilling, completion and estimated first
production date for all wells that are scheduled to be drilled in the foreseeable future.
In
addition, Oxy and ONEOK have conference calls, usually bi-weekly, to discuss connection
status of wells and changes to Oxy's drilling and completion schedules.
Gathering System
ONEOK's gathering system in this area is a dynamic system that has multiple compressor
stations with common suction lines. Gas produced from this pad will have a primary flow path
to ONEOK's Lodgepole compressor station and secondary flow paths to ONEOK's Killdeer and
Little Knife compressor stations. The actual flow of the gas will be based on compression
operating parameters and gathering system pressures. Gas gathered on this part of ONEOK's
gathering system is processed at ONEOK's Grassland Processing Plant located in Section 36,
T146N, R105W, McKenzie County, North Dakota.
In addition to ONEOK, Hiland has a low pressure gathering line approximately 1.5 miles west of
the Kary SWSE 24 Pad location and PetroHunt has a low pressure gathering line approximately
3.5 miles west of the Kary SWSE 24 Pad location. Hiland's and PetroHunt's lines, along with
ONEOK's, are shown on the attached map.
The production facilities for the Kary 6-24-13H-144-97 and State 4-25-36H-144-97 will be
located approximately 100' north of ONEOK's existing 8.625" outside diameter (OD) low
pressure gathering line. The connection to ONEOK will require approximately 100' of either
4.50" or 6.625" OD low pressure gathering line and related facilities.
Existing Lines
3
At the terminus of the metering, associated piping at each well's production facilities and the
100' of 4.50" or 6.625" OD low pressure gathering line noted above, a connection will be made
to an existing 8.625" OD gathering line. This 8.625" OD gathering line traverses approximately
one-half mile before connecting to a 12.75" OD gathering line. This 12.75" OD gathering line
traverses approximately 6.0 miles before connecting to a 16" OD gathering line. The gas then
travels approximately 35.0 miles before being compressed at ONEOK's Lodgepole compressor
station. This will be the primary flow path of gas delivered to ONEOK from this pad. As noted
under "Gathering System", above, the gas will have secondary flow paths due to the dynamics of
ONEOK's gathering system. The table below shows the capacities and current flows of the
primary gathering lines connecting this well.
ONEOK's low pressure gathering system is near capacity in this area due to continuing
development of the fields in this area. It is projected that the system will have capacity when this
well is ready for production due to decline on the existing wells gathered on this segment of the
system and ONEOK's continuing efforts to maximize flow on its gathering system(s).
ONEOK is in the process of adding compressors at its Lost Bridge compressor station in Section
14, T147N, R96W, Dunn County and installing a 16" OD low pressure gathering line that will
start in T145N, R94W, Dunn County (Dunn Center) and end at the inlet of the Lost Bridge
compressor station. Construction of these facilities will redirect gas that currently flows on the
primary and secondary flow paths of the Kary SWSE 24 Pad to flow on the new facilities.
Although this does not directly increase the capacity of the primary and secondary flow paths of
the Kary SWSE 24 Pad, it redirects gas that currently flows on the same pipelines to a different
compressor station, in essence reducing volumes transported on the flow paths for this well.
ONEOK is also planning on constructing a new discharge line from its Lost Bridge compressor
station that will deliver some of the gas currently processed at ONEOK's Grasslands Processing
Plant to ONEOK's Garden Creek Processing Plant(s).
ONEOK has announced plans to construct the Bear Creek natural gas processing plant and
related natural gas and natural gas liquids infrastructure in Dunn County, North Dakota. The
Bear Creek natural gas processing plant and related facilities are expected to be operation during
the second quarter of 2016. In addition, ONEOK Demicks Lake natural gas processing plant,
located in McKenzie County, North Dakota, is expected to be operational during the third quarter
of 2016.
Flowback Strategy
4
After the fracture treatment, these wells will be flowed through a choke to test production tanks.
Choke size will depend on final shut in pressure post frac and well pressure prior to opening the
choke. The choke will be adjusted up or down based on flowing pressure, liquid rates and sand
returns, to prevent clogging manifold chokes. During flowback, the water chlorides and sand
content will be monitored. When the water chlorides are greater than 100,000 ppm and the
produced fluids contain no sand, the wells will be turned to production facilities. Since the
pipeline is already at the location of the pad and Oxy will have its production facilities
constructed before flowback starts, and gas sales should start as soon as the wells start flowing
through the production facilities, unless there are capacity issues on ONEOK's system at that
time. Based on current information, it is our belief the system can take this gas upon completion
of the wells.
The typical well on this pad will initially flow 700 barrels of oil and 300 thousand cubic feet of
gas per day based on Oxy's production type curve of this area. Based on current drilling and
completion plans, these wells will be completed in the same timeframe. For the two wells, Oxy
projects a peak oil rate of 1,400 barrels and a peak gas rate of 600 thousand cubic feet per day
from the pad. It is anticipated these wells will decline sharply after initial production as do the
majority of horizontal wells in the Williston Basin.
Current Flaring
The table below shows gas produced and sold by Oxy per Gas Production Report - Form 5B that
was filed by Oxy for August 2014 reporting period. The percent sold and percent flared are also
shown in the table.
Flaring
Wells on this pad will be connected to a pipeline prior to production and Oxy does not expect to
flare gas. Below are three alternatives that Oxy considered from a conceptual standpoint to
reduce the amount of gas flared. More generally, Oxy is continuing to review the possible
impact of implementing one or more of these alternatives as appropriate in our operations.
1) NGL Removal ­ On Lease
Captures highest value components in gas stream
Plants are expensive
5
Uneconomical to operate when volume declines
Residue gas is still flared
2) Power Generation ­ On Lease
Savings if current generation's fuel supply is diesel
Only a portion of gas is consumed operating the generator, remainder of gas will
be flared
Due to gas quality, high NGL content, preference is to purchase power from the
grid and not operate generation on site
3) Compressed Natural Gas ­ On lease
Well site compressors are required to fill CNG trailers
Large capital outlay for equipment and operating cost, includes trucking of
products, are expensive
No gas would be flared, but might be uneconomical to operate when gas volume
declines

I, William H. Dolinar, Professional Land Surveyor, ND. RLS #6550, hereby certify that (in accordance with a request from Cody Dennison with Oxy USA, Inc., 3239 Highway
22, Dickinson, North Dakota 58601) I and/or personnel under my direction made a survey on the 14th day of July 2014, for the Surface Hole Location and Elevation of platted
well, being located within the SE1/4SE1/4 of Section 24, T144N, R97W of the 5th P.M., Dunn County, State of North Dakota.
Notes: All Azimuths are based on the South line of Section 24, T144N R97W of the 5th P.M., being an Azimuth of 269°41'29" using GPS observations, occupying a WHS control
point (5/8" rebar) and having the Location and Elevation derived from an OPUS Solution. Azimuths shown have been rotated 1°45'15.78538" West from SPC Grid bearings to
Geodetic North, based on convergence angle provided by a conversion using Corpscon.
Project elevations are held on the control point located 88°00'43", 503.54 Feet, from the South Quarter Corner of Section 24, T144N, R97W of the 5th P.M. having a NAVD 88
elevation of 2377.13 feet.
Distances shown are Ground Distances using a combined scale factor of 1.000142565.
Location shown here on is not an "ASBUILT" location.
